## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force depends nonlinearly on position x and may include explicit time-dependent driving. The equation of motion generalizes Hooke's law with anharmonic corrections and possible periodic forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic nonlinearity): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring)
- Asymmetric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity, asymmetric potential)
- General polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (sinusoidal external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear spring with driving)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated spring constant)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Driven with polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (asymmetric + driving)
- Inverse-cube force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 / x**3 (centrifugal-like effective potential)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (exact pendulum restoring torque)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear with multiple driving harmonics: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (multi-frequency forcing)
- Rational restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (saturating nonlinear spring)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential well, preserving x → -x symmetry
- Even-power terms (x**2) in restoring force → asymmetric potential, broken symmetry, indicates quadratic nonlinearity
- Periodic time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external driving force or parametric modulation
- Product x*cos(c*t) → parametric excitation where the effective spring constant oscillates in time
- sin(c*x) restoring force → pendulum-like dynamics with periodic potential (bounded restoring force)
- Cubic term x**3 with opposite sign to linear term → double-well (Duffing) potential with bistability
- Absence of velocity variable in acceleration equation → conservative system or velocity-independent forcing
- Rational function of x → saturating restoring force that limits growth at large displacements
